```markdown
# PVC Pipes
## Quick Facts
| Property | Value |
|---|---|

| **Price Range** | > 📭 No data found |

| **MOQ (Typical)** | Varies widely from small quantities (e.g., 150 feet) to bulk orders (800+ pieces) (buyer call data). |

## 1. Category Overview
### 1.1 Definition & Scope
PVC (Polyvinyl Chloride) Pipes are a type of plastic pipe used for conveying fluids, primarily water. They are a fundamental component in plumbing and infrastructure projects. The category encompasses pipes used for various applications including general plumbing, water mains, and irrigation. Buyer inquiries show a range from small-scale residential use to large, bulk industrial requirements (buyer call data).

### 1.2 Category Classification
-   **Parent Category**: Plumbing & Sanitation > Pipes & Fittings
-   **Sibling/Related Categories**: Based on buyer context, related categories include `Plumbing Pipe`, `Water Pipe`, and `Irrigation PVC Pipe` (buyer call data).

### 1.3 Market Context
The market for PVC Pipes in India serves both Business-to-Business (B2B) and Business-to-Consumer (B2C) segments.
-   **B2B Buyers**: Include manufacturers (e.g., Vijil Safety Technology) and contractors involved in industrial or construction projects requiring bulk quantities (e.g., 800 pipes) (buyer call data).
-   **B2C Buyers**: Typically end-customers or small-scale users purchasing smaller quantities (e.g., 150 feet) for residential applications (buyer call data).
-   **Geographic Spread**: Inquiries have been logged from various locations, including Jodhpur, Rajasthan, and Belgaum, Karnataka (buyer call data).

## 2. Product Types & Variants
### 2.1 Main Product Types
Based on initial call data, PVC pipes are primarily sought for their application. While specific product types are not yet detailed, common uses imply the existence of variants for:
-   **General Water Transportation:** For moving water in residential and commercial settings.
-   **Plumbing:** Standard pipes for plumbing systems.
-   **Irrigation:** Pipes suitable for agricultural water distribution, as suggested by related category analysis (`call 10.json`).

### 2.2 Available Sizes & Configurations
-   **Diameter**: 1.5 inches is a specific diameter requested by a buyer (`call 10.json`).
-   **Length/Quantity**: Pipes are procured in terms of length (e.g., "150 feet") and in discrete units (e.g., "800 pieces") (buyer call data).
```

- 🔍 **Query:** `IS code for unplasticized PVC pipes for agriculture India` (10 web results fetched)
  - **Rationale:** The source `call 16.json` mentions "ISI" certification for agricultural PVC pipes but does not provide the specific Indian Standard (IS) code number. To make the wiki more technically precise and useful for buyers, I need to find the specific IS code that governs the quality and specifications of PVC pipes used for agriculture in India.

<details><summary><b>View Structural Changes (Diff - Expand)</b></summary>

```diff
--- Before Update
+++ After Update
@@ -1 +1,5 @@
+<WEB_SEARCH_REASONING>
+<inferred>The web search successfully identified the specific Indian Standard (IS) codes associated with the "ISI" certification mentioned in the buyer call for agricultural pipes. The results differentiate between pipes for potable water/general use (`IS 4985`) and those specifically for agricultural pump suction/delivery lines (`IS 12231`). The search also confirmed that the pressure rating "4kg" and "6kg" mentioned in the call corresponds to the pressure classes of 0.4 MPa and 0.6 MPa defined in `IS 12231` (where 1kg/cm² ≈ 0.1 MPa).  ### 1.1 Definition & Scope
-PVC (Polyvinyl Chloride) Pipes are a type of plastic pipe used for conveying fluids, primarily water. They are a fundamental component in plumbing, infrastructure, borewells, and agricultural projects. The category encompasses pipes used for various applications including general plumbing, water mains, irrigation, drainage systems, and as conduits for electrical wiring in construction projects (`call 19.json`). Buyers often inquire about PVC pipes as part of a larger basket of construction materials, alongside HDPE pipes and conduits (`call 22.json`), and frequently require associated accessories like **fittings, bands, and joints** to create a complete system (`call 23.json`, `call 25.json`). +PVC (Polyvinyl Chloride) Pipes are a type of plastic pipe used for conveying fluids, primarily water. They are a fundamental component in plumbing, infrastructure, borewells, and agricultural projects. The category encompasses pipes used for various applications including general plumbing, water mains, irrigation, drainage systems, and as conduits for electrical wiring in construction projects (`call 19.json`). Products are typically made from Unplasticized PVC (uPVC) for rigidity and durability (`pdf 1.json`). Key features often highlighted by manufacturers include corrosion resistance, high flow capacity due to smooth walls, low installation cost, and long service life (over 50 years under proper use) (`pdf 10.json`).
```

```diff
-
```
```diff
--   **General Purpose / Plumbing Pipes**: Standard pipes for water transportation in residential and commercial settings. These are commonly requested in smaller diameters (1-3 inches).
```

```diff
 ### 6.1 Applicable Standards
-The "ISI" mark mentioned by sellers (`call 16.json`) refers to certification by the Bureau of Indian Standards (BIS). Web search results confirm the following key standards for uPVC pipes:
-
--   **IS 4985:2021 - Unplasticized PVC Pipes for Potable Water Supplies**: This is the primary standard for uPVC pipes used for carrying drinking water. It covers requirements for plain and socket-ended pipes. Though for potable water, pipes compliant with this standard are also marketed for general agricultural use [Web]. It specifies pressure classes, dimensions, and material properties.

+-   **Indian Standards (BIS)**:
+    -   **IS 4985:2021**: The primary standard for unplasticized PVC pipes for potable water supplies. An older version, `IS 4985-2000`, is also referenced by some manufacturers (`pdf 1.json`).
+    -   **IS 12818:1992**: Specifies requirements for uPVC Casing Pipes (CM and CS types) for borewells (`pdf 1.json`).
```

```diff
 **Analysis of New Sources:**
-*   **call 9.json:** Confirms B2B demand for large diameter pipes (10-12 inches) for irrigation and water transport in Gujarat. This reinforces existing buyer intelligence and adds a new buyer location.
-*   **pdf 1.json (VPL Catalog):** Introduces a new brand, `VPL`, and two specific product lines: Casing Pipes (conforming to the new standard `IS 12818:1992`) and Unplasticized PVC Pipes (conforming to `IS 4985-2000`). It provides extensive technical specifications for various sizes (100mm to 200mm) and formal pressure classes (Class 1 to 6, in MPa), which can be mapped to the vernacular "kg" ratings.
-*   **pdf 10.json (GUANGJIN Catalog):** Introduces an international manufacturer, `GUANGJIN` from China, adding an import dimension. It details PVC-U Pressure Pipes, highlighting a key classification: Plain End vs. Bell End. It provides a vast range of sizes (up to 630mm), new technical properties (Vicat Softening Temp, Specific Gravity), performance tests (Dichloromethane Resistance), ISO certifications, and a comprehensive list of applications and companion fittings.
+*   **pdf 11.json (Pressure Pipes):** This source details "Selfit" Unplasticized PVC Pressure Pipes conforming to IS 4985-2000. It provides a clear mapping between Pressure Classes (1-6), MPa ratings (0.25-1.25), and kgf/cm² ratings (2.5-12.5). It also introduces new international standards (ISO 161/1, ISO DIS 4422), a specific technical property (Safe working stress), and an extensive list of diameters (20-315mm).
+*   **pdf 12.json (Schedule Pipes):** This source introduces a new and important classification system for PVC pipes: **Schedule 40, 80, and 120**. It provides highly detailed wall thickness specifications for smaller diameter pipes (1/2" to 1 1/2") under this system.
+*   **pdf 2.json (SWR Pipes):** This source adds a new major product category: **SWR (Soil, Waste, and Rainwater) Pipes**, conforming to the new standard **IS 13592**. It details two joint types (SELFIT and RINGFIT) and two pipe types (Type A for rainwater/vents, Type B for soil/waste). It provides comprehensive dimensional specifications for various nominal diameters (DN 75-160mm). A data inconsistency in this source regarding the diameter of DN 110 pipes will be noted and flagged with a doubt.

 ### 1.1 Definition & Scope
-PVC (Polyvinyl Chloride) Pipes are a type of plastic pipe used for conveying fluids, primarily water. They are a fundamental component in plumbing, infrastructure, borewells, and agricultural projects. The category encompasses pipes used for various applications including general plumbing, water mains, irrigation, drainage systems, and as conduits for electrical wiring in construction projects (`call 19.json`). Products are typically made from Unplasticized PVC (uPVC) for rigidity and durability (`pdf 1.json`). Key features often highlighted by manufacturers include corrosion resistance, high flow capacity due to smooth walls, low installation cost, and long service life (over 50 years under proper use) (`pdf 10.json`).
+PVC (Polyvinyl Chloride) Pipes are a type of plastic pipe used for conveying fluids (primarily water) and waste. They are a fundamental component in plumbing, infrastructure, borewells, and agricultural projects. The category encompasses pipes for various applications including general plumbing, potable water mains, irrigation, **Soil, Waste, and Rainwater (SWR) drainage systems**, and as conduits for electrical wiring in construction projects (`call 19.json`, `pdf 2.json`). Products are typically made from Unplasticized PVC (uPVC) for rigidity and durability (`pdf 1.json`). Key features often highlighted by manufacturers include corrosion resistance, high flow capacity due to smooth walls, low installation cost, and long service life (over 50 years under proper use) (`pdf 10.json`).

 ### 3.2 Specification Interdependencies
--   **Pressure, Weight, and Price**: For a given diameter, a higher pressure rating (e.g., 6 kg/cm² or 0.6 MPa) requires thicker walls, resulting in a heavier and more expensive pipe compared to a lower rating (e.g., 4 kg/cm² or 0.4 MPa) (`call 16.json`).
+-   **Pressure, Weight, and Price**: For a given diameter, a higher pressure rating (e.g., 6 kg/cm² or 0.6 MPa) requires thicker walls, resulting in a heavier and more expensive pipe compared to a lower rating (e.g., 4 kg/cm² or 0.4 MPa) (`call 16.json`). This is also demonstrated in Schedule pipes, where higher schedules (e.g. Sch 80 vs Sch 40) have thicker walls for the same nominal size (`pdf 12.json`).
+-   **SWR Type A vs. Type B**: For SWR pipes of the same diameter, Type B has a significantly thicker wall than Type A, as it is designed for carrying solid waste, while Type A is for rainwater and ventilation (`pdf 2.json`).
```

```diff
 ### 1.1 Definition & Scope
-PVC (Polyvinyl Chloride) Pipes are a type of plastic pipe used for conveying fluids (primarily water) and waste. They are a fundamental component in plumbing, infrastructure, borewells, and agricultural projects. The category encompasses pipes for various applications including general plumbing, potable water mains, irrigation, **Soil, Waste, and Rainwater (SWR) drainage systems**, and as conduits for electrical wiring in construction projects (`call 19.json`, `pdf 2.json`). Products are typically made from Unplasticized PVC (uPVC) for rigidity and durability (`pdf 1.json`). Key features often highlighted by manufacturers include corrosion resistance, high flow capacity due to smooth walls, low installation cost, and long service life (over 50 years under proper use) (`pdf 10.json`).
+PVC (Polyvinyl Chloride) Pipes are a type of plastic pipe used for conveying fluids (primarily water) and waste. They are a fundamental component in plumbing, infrastructure, borewells, and agricultural projects. The category encompasses pipes for various applications including general plumbing, potable water mains, irrigation, **Soil, Waste, and Rainwater (SWR) drainage systems**, and as conduits for electrical wiring in construction projects (`call 19.json`, `pdf 2.json`).
+
+Products are typically made from Unplasticized PVC (uPVC) for rigidity and durability; some variants are **UV-Stabilized** to protect against sunlight degradation (`pdf 1.json`, `pdf 4.json`). Key features often highlighted by manufacturers include corrosion resistance, acid/alkali-proof properties, excellent electrical insulation, high flow capacity due to smooth walls (low friction), low installation cost, and long service life (over 50 years under proper use) (`pdf 10.json`, `pdf 3.json`, `pdf 4.json`).

 ### 3.2 Specification Interdependencies
--   **Pressure, Weight, and Price**: For a given diameter, a higher pressure rating (e.g., 6 kg/cm² or 0.6 MPa) requires thicker walls, resulting in a heavier and more expensive pipe compared to a lower rating (e.g., 4 kg/cm² or 0.4 MPa) (`call 16.json`). This is also demonstrated in Schedule pipes, where higher schedules (e.g. Sch 80 vs Sch 40) have thicker walls for the same nominal size (`pdf 12.json`).
+-   **Pressure, Weight, and Price**: For a given diameter, a higher pressure rating (e.g., 6 kg/cm², PN 1.0, Sch 80) requires thicker walls, resulting in a heavier and more expensive pipe compared to a lower rating (e.g., 4 kg/cm², PN 0.63, Sch 40) (`call 16.json`, `pdf 12.json`, `pdf 3.json`).
 -   **SWR Type A vs. Type B**: For SWR pipes of the same diameter, Type B has a significantly thicker wall than Type A, as it is designed for carrying solid waste, while Type A is for rainwater and ventilation (`pdf 2.json`).
--   **Standard vs. Available Size**: Large diameter pipes (e.g., 10-12 inches) are requested by buyers for applications like irrigation and mains, but may not be stocked by all suppliers (`call 8.json`). However, manufacturer catalogs confirm production up to 630mm (~25 inches), indicating they are available from primary sources (`pdf 10.json`).
+-   **Standard vs. Available Size**: Large diameter pipes (e.g., 10-12 inches) are requested by buyers, and manufacturer catalogs confirm production up to 630mm (~25 inches), indicating they are available from primary sources even if not stocked by all distributors (`call 8.json`, `pdf 3.json`).
 -   **End Type and Installation**: The choice between a Plain/Selfit End pipe and a Bell/Ringfit End pipe dictates the installation method: solvent welding versus a gasketed push-fit joint.
```

```diff
 ### 3.2 Specification Interdependencies
--   **Pressure, Weight, and Price**: For a given diameter, a higher pressure rating (e.g., 6 kg/cm², PN 1.0, Sch 80) requires thicker walls, resulting in a heavier and more expensive pipe compared to a lower rating (e.g., 4 kg/cm², PN 0.63, Sch 40) (`call 16.json`, `pdf 12.json`, `pdf 3.json`).
+-   **Pressure, Wall Thickness, and Weight**: For a given diameter, a higher pressure rating (e.g., Class 3 / 6 kg/cm²) requires a thicker wall than a lower rating (e.g., Class 1 / 2.5 kg/cm²). This increases the material content, weight, and price of the pipe (`call 16.json`, `pdf 8.json`).
 -   **SWR Type A vs. Type B**: For SWR pipes of the same diameter, Type B has a significantly thicker wall than Type A, as it is designed for carrying solid waste, while Type A is for rainwater and ventilation (`pdf 2.json`).
--   **Standard vs. Available Size**: Large diameter pipes (e.g., 10-12 inches) are requested by buyers, and manufacturer catalogs confirm production up to 630mm (~25 inches), indicating they are available from primary sources even if not stocked by all distributors (`call 8.json`, `pdf 3.json`).
--   **End Type and Installation**: The choice between a Plain/Selfit End pipe and a Bell/Ringfit End pipe dictates the installation method: solvent welding versus a gasketed push-fit joint.
+-   **Standard vs. Available Size**: Large diameter pipes (e.g., 10-12 inches) are requested by buyers, and manufacturer catalogs confirm production up to 400mm (~16 inches), indicating they are available from primary sources even if not stocked by all distributors (`call 8.json`, `pdf 7.json`).
```

```diff
 ### 1.1 Definition & Scope
-PVC (Polyvinyl Chloride) Pipes are a type of plastic pipe used for conveying fluids (primarily water) and waste. They are a fundamental component in plumbing, infrastructure, borewells, and agricultural projects. The category encompasses pipes for various applications including general plumbing, potable water mains, irrigation, **Soil, Waste, and Rainwater (SWR) drainage systems**, and as conduits for electrical wiring in construction projects (`call 19.json`, `pdf 2.json`).
+PVC (Polyvinyl Chloride) Pipes are a type of plastic pipe used for conveying fluids (primarily water) and waste. They are a fundamental component in plumbing, infrastructure, borewells, and agricultural projects.  ### 1.1 Definition & Scope
```
-PVC (Polyvinyl Chloride) Pipes are a type of plastic pipe used for conveying fluids (primarily water) and waste. They are a fundamental component in plumbing, infrastructure, borewells, and agricultural projects. The category encompasses pipes for various applications including general plumbing, potable water mains, irrigation, **Soil, Waste, and Rainwater (SWR) drainage systems**, **column pipes for submersible pump installations**, and as conduits for electrical wiring in construction projects (`call 19.json`, `pdf 2.json`, `pdf 9.json`).
-
-Products are typically made from Unplasticized PVC (uPVC) for rigidity and durability, often from raw materials like **suspension grade PVC resin** (`pdf 7.json`). Some variants are **UV-Stabilized** to protect against sunlight degradation (`pdf 1.json`, `pdf 4.json`). Key features often highlighted by manufacturers include corrosion resistance, acid/alkali-proof properties, excellent electrical insulation, high flow capacity due to smooth walls (low friction), low installation cost, and long service life (over 50 years under proper use) (`pdf 10.json`, `pdf 3.json`, `pdf 4.json`).
+Polyvinyl Chloride (PVC) Pipes are a versatile and widely used type of plastic pipe primarily for conveying water and other fluids. As a fundamental component in modern infrastructure, they are essential for plumbing, irrigation, and sanitation projects. The category primarily consists of pipes made from Unplasticized PVC (uPVC or PVC-U), a rigid and durable material ideal for pressure applications. Some variants are made from `[[PVC-Resin]]` that is UV-stabilized to prevent degradation from sunlight, a crucial feature for agricultural and surface applications (`pdf 1.json`, `pdf 4.json`).
+
+The product scope is broad, covering everything from drinking water supply and agricultural irrigation to specialized uses. Key sub-categories include **uPVC Pressure Pipes** for water mains, **uPVC Column Pipes** designed for high-tensile loads in `[[Submersible-Pump]]` installations, **SWR (Soil, Waste, and Rainwater) Pipes** for drainage, and **Casing Pipes** for lining borewells (`pdf 2.json`, `pdf 9.json`). Manufacturers consistently highlight features such as corrosion resistance, smooth internal walls for high flow rates, low installation costs, and a long service life often exceeding 50 years (`pdf 10.json`, `pdf 3.json`, `pdf 4.json`).

 ### 2.1 Main Product Types
-Based on buyer inquiries and manufacturer catalogs, several distinct types of PVC pipes are available:
-
--   **Unplasticized PVC (uPVC/PVC-U) Pressure Pipes**: The most common type, used for potable water supply, irrigation (feedwater), and industrial fluid transport. They are classified by pressure ratings and conform to standards like IS 4985. They can have different joint types (`pdf 1.json`, `pdf 10.json`, `pdf 11.json`, `pdf 3.json`, `pdf 6.json`).
--   **uPVC Column Pipes**: Specialized high-tensile pipes designed to be used as the riser pipe for submersible pumps in borewells. They are characterized by high load-bearing capacity, special threads (e.g., square threads), and locking mechanisms to prevent pipes from detaching during operation. They are often available in "Standard" and "Heavy" grades to suit different pump depths and weights (`pdf 9.json`).
--   **SWR (Soil, Waste, and Rainwater) Pipes**: Specifically designed for drainage systems in buildings, conforming to IS 13592. They are not intended for pressure applications.
-    -   **Type A**: Used for ventilating and rainwater harvesting applications.
-    -   **Type B**: Used for soil and waste discharge applications, featuring thicker walls for higher strength. (`pdf 2.json`)
--   **Schedule Pipes (Sch 40, 80, 120)**: A classification system (often per ASTM-D 1785) where pipes of a given nominal size have a standard outside diameter, but wall thickness increases from Schedule 40 to 80 to 120, allowing for higher pressure handling. Used in plumbing, irrigation and industrial applications (`pdf 12.json`, `pdf 4.json`).
--   **Clear PVC Pipes**: A specialized variant, typically made to Schedule 40 dimensions, that offers excellent transparency. These are used in applications where visual monitoring of fluid flow is required, such as sight glasses, double containment systems, and low-pressure process piping (`pdf 5.json`).
--   **CM & CS Casing Pipes**: Specifically designed for borewell applications, conforming to IS 12818. CM stands for Casing Medium-duty and CS for Casing Shallow-well (`pdf 1.json`, `pdf 7.json`).
--   **PVC Agriculture Pipes**: Designed for irrigation and agricultural pump sets, often specified by diameter and a "kg" pressure rating. These are typically ISI marked (`call 16.json`, `IS 12231`).
--   **PVC Conduit Pipes**: Used as protective casing for electrical wiring in construction (`call 19.json`, `call 22.json`).
--   **Classification by Joint Type**:
-    -   **Plain End / Selfit (Solvent Weld)**: Pipes with straight ends (Plain) or one self-socketed end (Selfit). Both are designed to be joined using solvent cement to form a permanent, watertight joint. Self-socketed ends can reduce installation time and solvent cement usage by 50% (`pdf 7.json`, `pdf 10.json`, `pdf 11.json`, `pdf 2.json`).
-    -   **Bell End / Ringfit (Gasketed)**: Pipes with one flared end ("bell") containing an integral groove to hold a rubber gasket. This allows for a push-fit, trouble-free watertight joint that accommodates thermal expansion and contraction (`pdf 10.json`, `pdf 2.json`).
-

+PVC pipes are categorized based on their application, material properties, and jointing method.
+
+-   **Unplasticized PVC (uPVC/PVC-U) Pressure Pipes**: The most common type, used for potable water supply, irrigation, and industrial fluid transport. They are classified by pressure ratings (kg/cm² or Classes) and conform to **IS 4985**. They are joined using `[[Solvent-Cement]]` or gasketed joints (`pdf 1.json`, `pdf 11.json`).
+-   **uPVC Column Pipes**: Specialized high-tensile pipes designed as the riser pipe for `[[Submersible-Pump]]` installations in borewells. Their key features are high load-bearing capacity, precision-machined square threads, and locking mechanisms to prevent detachment. They are typically available in "Standard" and "Heavy" grades to suit various pump depths and weights (`pdf 9.json`).
+-   **SWR (Soil, Waste, and Rainwater) Pipes**: Designed for gravity-fed drainage systems in buildings, conforming to **IS 13592**. Not suitable for pressure applications.
+    -   **Type A**: Used for ventilating stacks and rainwater harvesting.
+    -   **Type B**: Have thicker walls for higher strength, used for discharging soil and waste (`pdf 2.json`).
+-   **Schedule Pipes (Sch 40, 80, 120)**: Classified per **ASTM D1785**, these pipes have a standard outside diameter for a given size, but wall thickness increases with the schedule number, enabling higher pressure tolerance. Common in industrial applications and plumbing (`pdf 12.json`, `pdf 4.json`).
+-   **Clear PVC Pipes**: A transparent variant, typically with Schedule 40 dimensions, used in applications requiring visual monitoring of fluid flow, such as sight glasses, lab work, and low-pressure process lines (`pdf 5.json`).
+-   **CM & CS Casing Pipes**: Designed specifically for borewell construction, conforming to **IS 12818**. CM (Casing Medium) is for medium-depth wells, and CS (Casing Shallow) is for shallower wells (`pdf 1.json`, `pdf 7.json`).
+-   **PVC Agriculture (Agri) Pipes**: Intended for irrigation and agricultural pump sets, typically ISI marked and specified by diameter and a "kg" pressure rating (`call 16.json`, `IS 12231`).
+-   **PVC Conduit Pipes**: Used as a protective casing for `[[Electrical-Wire]]` systems in construction (`call 19.json`, `call 22.json`).
+
+### 2.2 Classification by Joint Type
+-   **Plain End / Selfit (Solvent Weld)**: Pipes with either straight ends (Plain) oder one factory-formed socketed end (Selfit). Both are permanently joined using `[[Solvent-Cement]]`. Selfit pipes can reduce installation time and `[[Solvent-Cement]]` consumption by up to 50% (`pdf 7.json`).
+-   **Bell End / Ringfit (Gasketed)**: Pipes with one flared "bell" end containing a groove for a `[[Rubber-Gasket]]`. This creates a push-fit, leak-proof seal that accommodates thermal expansion and contraction, common in SWR and underground water mains (`pdf 10.json`, `pdf 2.json`).

 ### 3.2 Specification Interdependencies
--   **Pressure, Wall Thickness, and Weight**: For a given diameter of pressure pipe, a higher pressure rating (e.g., Class 3 / 6 kg/cm²) requires a thicker wall than a lower rating (e.g., Class 1 / 2.5 kg/cm²). This increases the material content, weight, and price of the pipe (`call 16.json`, `pdf 8.json`).
--   **Column Pipe Grade & Performance**: For a given diameter of column pipe, the "Heavy" grade has significantly higher Ultimate Breaking Load, Safe Pulling Load, and can support a greater Pump Delivery Head compared to the "Standard" grade (`pdf 9.json`).
--   **SWR Type A vs. Type B**: For SWR pipes of the same diameter, Type B has a significantly thicker wall than Type A, as it is designed for carrying solid waste, while Type A is for rainwater and ventilation (`pdf 2.json`).
--   **Standard vs. Available Size**: Large diameter pipes (e.g., 10-12 inches) are requested by buyers, and manufacturer catalogs confirm production up to 400mm (~16 inches), indicating they are available from primary sources even if not stocked by all distributors (`call 8.json`, `pdf 7.json`).
--   **End Type and Installation**: The choice between a Plain/Selfit End pipe and a Bell/Ringfit End pipe dictates the installation method: solvent welding versus a gasketed push-fit joint. Self-socketed pipes are marketed as reducing labor time and solvent cement usage by up to 50% (`pdf 7.json`).
+-   **Pressure, Wall Thickness, and Cost**: For a given diameter, a higher pressure rating (e.g., Class 3 / 6 kg/cm²) necessitates a thicker wall, which increases the material weight and a pipe's per-meter cost (`call 16.json`, `pdf 8.json`).
+-   **Column Pipe Grade & Performance**: A "Heavy" grade column pipe has a thicker wall than a "Standard" grade of the same diameter. This results in a significantly higher Ultimate Breaking Load, Safe Pulling Load, and allows it to support a greater Pump Delivery Head, making it suitable for deeper borewells (`pdf 9.json`).
+-   **SWR Type A vs. Type B**: For SWR drainage pipes, Type B has a thicker wall than Type A of the same diameter, providing the necessary strength for carrying soil and solid waste, while Type A is sufficient for rainwater and ventilation (`pdf 2.json`).
+-   **Joint Type & Application**: Ringfit (gasketed) joints are preferred for buried non-pressure lines (like main drains) as they handle soil movement and thermal expansion. Selfit (solvent weld) joints form a rigid, monolithic structure ideal for above-ground plumbing and pressure lines.

 ### 7.2 Specific Use Cases
--   **Submersible Pump Installation**: uPVC Column pipes (e.g., Nandi Gold) are used as the riser main to connect a submersible pump inside a borewell to the surface. Their high tensile strength, safe pulling load, and special locking threads are critical for safely supporting the pump's weight and operational torque (`pdf 9.json`).
--   **Piped Irrigation Efficiency**: Using PVC pipes for field irrigation can improve water utilization to 0.95 (vs. channels), save 20-30% in power, and reduce land use by 2-3% (`pdf 3.json`).

Their high tensile strength (Safe Pulling Load) and robust square threads are critical for supporting the pump's weight and operational torque without failure (`pdf 9.json`).
+-   **Efficient Irrigation**: Using PVC pipes for irrigation can increase water utilization to 95% compared to open channels, saving 20-30% in power and reducing land use (`pdf 3.json`).
+-   **Visual Process Monitoring**: Clear PVC pipes serve as "sight glasses" in industrial systems, allowing operators to visually confirm fluid flow, color, and clarity without halting the process (`pdf 5.json`).

 ### 8.3 Storage
-> 📭 **No data found in current sources.**
+> Proper storage is crucial to maintain pipe integrity and prevent damage. Based on industry best practices [Web]:
+> -   **Support**: Store pipes on a level, flat surface. Use horizontal wooden battens spaced no more than 1 meter apart to prevent sagging. Do not store directly on uneven ground.
+> -   **Stacking**: Stack pipes in layers, with larger diameters at the bottom. To prevent deformation of the lower layers, the stack height should not exceed 1.5 meters.
+> -   **Protection**: Protect pipes from direct sunlight to prevent UV degradation, which can make them brittle. If stored outdoors, cover the stack with a light-colored, opaque tarp that allows for air circulation. Avoid dark tarps that absorb heat.
+> -   **Handling**: Avoid dropping pipes or dragging them on rough surfaces. Keep them away from sharp objects, hot surfaces, and heavy machinery.
+> -   **Inventory**: Practice "First-In, First-Out" (FIFO) to ensure older stock is used first.

-### 9.4 Market Trends & Outlook
-- **Dynamic Pricing**: The market is characterized by daily price fluctuations, likely tied to raw material costs (`call 4.json`).
-- **Focus on Efficiency**: Manufacturers are promoting product features that save installation time and material costs, such as self-socketed pipes which can reduce labor and solvent cement requirements by 50% (`pdf 7.json`).
-- **Specialization**: Emergence of highly specialized products like Column Pipes with specific performance features (locking threads, high tensile strength) indicates a mature market with targeted solutions (`pdf 9.json`).
+- **Buyer Archetypes**:
+    - **Contractors & Builders**: Procure large volumes for infrastructure and real estate projects. Key criteria are compliance with standards (IS codes), reliable supply, and competitive bulk pricing.
+    - **Wholesalers & Distributors**: Buy in bulk from manufacturers to stock inventory. They prioritize brand dealership, distributor margins, and product portfolio range (pipes + fittings).
+    - **Farmers**: Purchase Agri and Casing pipes for irrigation and borewells. Key criteria are the ISI mark, pressure rating (kg), and local availability at an affordable price.
+    - **Industrial Procurers**: Require specialized pipes (e.g., Sch 80, Clear PVC) for chemical transport or process lines. They focus on material specifications, chemical resistance, and temperature ratings.
+
+- **Demand Signals & Top Requested Specs**:
+    1.  **Brand**: High demand for Tier 1 brands `Supreme` and `Ashirvad`.
+    2.  **Pipe Type**: Strong demand for `Agricultural Pipes`, `SWR Pipes`, and increasingly specialized `Column Pipes`.
+    3.  **Diameter**: Common requests are for 75mm (3"), 100mm (4"), 250mm (10"), and 315mm (12").
+    4.  **Pressure Rating**: For Agri/Pressure pipes, `4 kg/cm²` and `6 kg/cm²` are the most frequently specified ratings.
+    5.  **Length**: Standard lengths of `10 feet` (~3m) and `20 feet` (~6m) are most common.
+
+- **Price Trends & Analysis**:
+    - Prices are highly volatile, with sellers confirming daily rate changes. This is primarily driven by fluctuations in the global price of `[[PVC-Resin]]`.
+    - A clear price premium exists for higher-specification products. For example, a 6 kg pressure pipe can be up to 45% more expensive than a 4 kg pipe of the same diameter (`call 16.json`).
+    - Pricing is typically quoted inclusive of GST, but logistics costs are almost always quoted separately and can be a significant portion of the total cost.
+
+- **Competitive Landscape**:
+    - **Intra-Category**: Fierce competition exists between Tier 1 brands (Supreme, Ashirvad) and a large number of Tier 2 national and regional players (Finolex, Plasto, Kothari).
+    - **Inter-Category**: For certain applications, PVC pipes compete with `[[HDPE-Pipe]]` (more flexible, used in gas lines) and `[[CPVC-Pipe]]` (higher temperature resistance, used in hot water plumbing).
+    - **Value Proposition**: Suppliers offering a complete solution—a wide range of pipes plus all necessary `[[PVC-Pipe-Fittings]]`, valves, and cements—have a strong competitive edge.
+
+- **Regional Patterns & Procurement Insights**:
+    - Supply is concentrated in industrial states like Gujarat and Rajasthan, but distribution networks are crucial for national reach.
+    - High freight costs strongly favor local sourcing. Buyers in remote areas will almost always choose a local distributor, even if the base price is higher, to avoid prohibitive shipping charges.
+    - The typical procurement cycle for SME buyers is fast-paced and digitally enabled, moving from a phone call directly to sharing catalogs and rate lists on WhatsApp.

 ### 10.3 Common Concerns & Objections
--   **High Freight Costs**: A major concern and deal-breaker for small or long-distance orders (`call 5.json`, `call 7.json`).
--   **Supplier Stock Limitation**: A friction point when a supplier doesn't stock required sizes, especially large diameters or specific types (`call 8.json`, `call 15.json`).
--   **Information Exchange**: Buyers expect quick sharing of product details, pricing, and photos on WhatsApp.
+-   **High Freight Costs**: The most frequent reason for a deal falling through for non-local suppliers (`call 5.json`, `call 7.json`).
+-   **Stock Availability**: Frustration when a supplier does not stock the required size (especially large diameters) or specific type (e.g., Schedule 120).
+-   **Minimum Order Quantity (MOQ)**: Mismatch between supplier's bulk MOQ and buyer's smaller requirement.
+-   **Information Lag**: Delays in receiving a rate list or catalogue can lead buyers to seek other suppliers.

-| **Pump Delivery Head** | The maximum vertical distance (in meters) that a pump can push water through a specific column pipe system. |
-| **Ringfit Joint** | A type of joint for SWR pipes with a socket end holding a rubber gasket for a push-fit, watertight seal that allows thermal expansion. |
-| **Safe Pulling Load** | The maximum tensile load (in kgf) that can be safely applied to a column pipe during installation or operation without risk of failure. This accounts for the pump's weight and water column. |
-| **Schedule 40/80/120** | A standard for pipe dimensions (e.g., ASTM-D 1785). For a given size, the outside diameter is fixed, but the wall thickness increases with the schedule number. |
-| **Selfit Joint** | A type of solvent weld joint where one end of the pipe is self-socketed, allowing it to fit over the plain end of another pipe without a separate coupler. |
-| **Square Threads** | A type of screw thread with a square cross-section, known for high load-bearing capacity and efficiency, often used in high-load applications like column pipes. |

-| **uPVC** | Unplasticized Polyvinyl Chloride. A rigid form of PVC used for pipes due to its stiffness and durability. |
-| **UV Stabilized** | A material that includes additives to protect it from the long-term degradation effects of ultraviolet light from the sun. |
-| **Vicat Softening Temp.**| The temperature at which a plastic starts to soften rapidly under a specific load. A measure of heat resistance. |
